Homestead Capital, which invests in U.S. farmland, said it held a final closing for its second vehicle at $400 million. Homestead Capital USA Farmland Fund II LP hit its hard cap and surpassed an original target of $350 million. Limited partners include public pension funds, endowments, foundations, insurance companies and funds of funds. Many of the fund's backers were returning investors from the firm's debut vehicle, said Gabe Santos, a co-founder and portfolio manager at Homestead. The firm's first fund closed in 2015 with $173 million. Investors in the firm's debut vehicle included the Teacher Retirement System of Texas, Flag Capital Management, Meketa Investment Group and the University of Alabama, Private Equity Analyst previously reported. The firm, which owns a portfolio of farms in 11 states that produce 16 different crops, said it would continue to invest in farmland throughout the Mountain West, Pacific, Midwest and Delta regions.

Huron Capital Partners, Detroit

Huron Capital Partners is targeting $100 million for Huron Flex Equity Fund LP, according to a Securities and Exchange Commission filing. The firm in April launched a new strategy called Flex Equity to take minority stakes in lower midmarket companies. Huron at the time said the strategy would invest $20 million to $200 million in U.S. and Canadian companies within its focus sectors: business services, consumer products and services, specialty manufacturing and health care. The firm's investments this year include Good Sportsman Marketing LLC, which makes hunting accessories, and InterVision Systems LLC, a provider of information-technology infrastructure.

Juniper Capital Advisors, Houston

Juniper Capital Advisors hit the $500 million hard cap for its second fund, Juniper Capital II LP. The firm's first fund was a friends-and-family vehicle that gathered $90 million in 2003. Juniper invests in lower midmarket upstream oil and gas companies in the U.S., aiming to deploy $25 million to $75 million per deal. It so far has made five investments from the fund, using about half of its capital, said Managing Partner Edward Geiser. The fund held a first close in November 2015 with a number of energy investors, said Terence Crikelair, managing partner at placement agent Champlain Advisors LLC.

Kainos Capital, Dallas

Kainos Capital closed Kainos Capital Partners II LP at the fund's $895 million hard cap, more than the $475 million its debut fund gathered in 2013. The new fund was seeking $750 million, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The lower midmarket investor operates primarily in the food and consumer sectors and generally invests $50 million to $150 million per deal. Texas Municipal Retirement System committed $50 million to the fund, according to a pension document. Kainos raised the fund in seven months and hasn't yet started investing from the vehicle, said a person familiar with the matter.

Leeds Equity Partners, New York

Leeds Equity Partners is targeting $750 million for Leeds Equity Partners VI LP and could collect as much as $1 billion, according to an investor memorandum. The firm's last fund was launched in 2008, the same year as the collapse of Lehman Brothers Holdings Inc. It targeted $1 billion in investor money for Leeds Equity Partners V LP, but ultimately closed on $522 million two years later, according to regulatory filings and investor documents. The firm received a pledge for its latest fund from the National Treasury Management Agency, which manages funds for the government of Ireland. Leeds Equity announced an exit this year with the sale of Evanta Ventures Inc., which provides opportunities for C-suite executives to network and collaborate.

Morgenthaler Private Equity, Cleveland

Morgenthaler Private Equity closed MPE Partners II LP at its $250 million hard cap. The firm said more than 30 investors committed to the oversubscribed fund. The vehicle will invest in industrial manufacturing and services companies. Morgenthaler invests in North American companies with annual earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization in excess of $5 million and enterprise values of $25 million to $150 million.

NewSpring Capital, Radnor, Pa.

NewSpring Capital collected at least $253.8 million so far for its fourth technology-focused growth-equity fund, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The firm aims to raise $300 million for NewSpring Growth Capital IV LP, according to the filing. The vehicle's size is a step up from its predecessor, which closed at $250 million in 2013. NewSpring's growth capital funds invest in growth-stage business services and technology companies in the mid-Atlantic U.S. that generate annual revenue of $5 million and $50 million.

Oncap, Toronto

Oncap, the midmarket investing arm of Toronto-based Onex Corp., so far raised nearly $1.09 billion for its fourth fund, Oncap IV LP, and a related vehicle, according to filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The fund exceeded the size of the 800 million Canadian dollar Oncap III LP, which closed in 2011. Midmarket-focused Oncap is one of Onex's two private-equity platforms, along with Onex Partners, which buys larger businesses. Oncap buys North American businesses valued at C$50 million to C$500 million.

ParkerGale Capital, Chicago

ParkerGale Capital, which invests in software and technology-enabled services, said it raised $240 million for its first buyout vehicle. The fund, ParkerGale Capital LP, exceeded its original target of $200 million. Devin Mathews, a partner at ParkerGale, said the fund also surpassed the $225 million cap that was set when the firm began its fundraising efforts in January 2015. Family offices, pensions, managed accounts, funds of funds and endowments contributed to the fund. Mr. Mathews said 12 institutions invested in the firm's first fund. The vehicle is expected to fund six or seven investments in the coming years and aims to back two new platform companies a year, he said. The firm has so far invested from the vehicle in two businesses: Aircraft Technical Publishers, an information management and service provider for the aviation industry; and OnePlus Corp., a sensor and software business for the waste management industry, retailers, municipalities and property owners. ParkerGale invests $20 million to $40 million in companies with $10 million to $30 million of revenue, Mr. Mathews said.

Rockland Capital, The Woodlands, Texas

Rockland Capital gathered at least $152.5 million so far for its third fund, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. Rockland Power Partners III LP has a $450 million target and a $500 million hard cap, according to the filing. The firm's last fund closed at $425 million in 2013. Rockland invests in power and energy infrastructure in North America and Europe, and has made deals in natural gas, coal, oil, solar and wind projects, among other types of energy-generation infrastructure. The firm in September agreed to buy two power facilities in Nevada and Florida from Quantum Utility Generation LLC.

Stripes Group, New York

Stripes Group is seeking $750 million for SG Growth Partners IV LP, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The offering amount for the firm's latest fund exceeds the $500 million the growth-equity investor raised for Stripes' third fund in 2014. Investors that disclosed commitments to that vehicle include the Board of Regents of the University of Michigan, Los Angeles City Employees' Retirement System and Los Angeles Fire and Police Pensions. Stripes typically makes growth-equity investments of $10 million to $150 million in internet, software, health-care information-technology and branded consumer-products businesses. The firm's portfolio includes online giving platform GoFundMe Inc.; meal-delivery company Blue Apron Inc.; fashion website operator and digital media company Refinery29 Inc.; and natural beverage business Califa Farms.

DISTRESSED/TURNAROUND

Atlantic Street Capital, Stamford, Conn.

Atlantic Street Capital held a final closing for Atlantic Street Capital III LP with $210 million of committed capital, surpassing a $200 million target. The firm, which invests in companies in the lower midmarket with a focus on entrepreneur and family-owned businesses, makes equity commitments of $10 million to $30 million in North American companies with earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization of $4 million to $12 million.

MEZZANINE & OTHER DEBT

Audax Group, Boston

Audax Group hit the $500 million hard cap for its third senior loan fund. The vehicle has more than triple that amount to invest, however, with a $1.1 billion credit facility it secured for the vehicle. The final closing of Audax Senior Loan Fund III LP came in ahead of a $400 million target for equity commitments. Audax's senior debt group targets loans for midmarket companies with $10 million to $50 million of earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization. It plans to focus the fund on first-lien senior secured loans to U.S. midmarket businesses as part of private equity-backed deals. The closing for Audax's third senior debt fund follows close on the heels of a fundraising for Audax Mezzanine Fund IV LP, which closed with about $1.2 billion earlier this year.

Carlyle Group LP, Washington

Carlyle Group LP raised $2.8 billion for its second energy mezzanine fund. The final closing of Carlyle Energy Mezzanine Opportunities Fund II LP came in at more than double the size of its predecessor fund, which wrapped up with $1.38 billion in 2012. The fund had a $2.5 billion target, according to due diligence notes for the Pennsylvania Public School Employees' Retirement System, which approved a commitment of up to $250 million to the fund in 2014. Carlyle plans to invest the fund in projects and companies in the power generation and energy sectors with a focus on companies requiring $50 million to $500 million of capital per deal.

Falcon Investment Advisors, Boston

Falcon Investment Advisors secured at least $842.6 million for its fifth fund, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The fund, Falcon Strategic Partners V LP, has a $1.25 billion target and a $1.5 billion hard cap, Private Equity Analyst previously reported. The firm's fourth fund closed on $910 million in 2014. Falcon provides $25 million to $75 million of capital through subordinated debt, preferred stock or noncontrol common equity to companies with more than $10 million in earnings before interest, taxes depreciation and amortization. Falcon in August invested in CXtec, which sells refurbished information-technology supplies, and CardConnect Corp., a payment processor, in July. The firm in October agreed to sell its stake in Triad Retail Media, an online advertising company.

Freeport Financial Partners, Chicago

Freeport Financial Partners, a direct lender that is part of investment bank Moelis & Co.'s asset-management arm, closed its third fund, Freeport First Lien Loan Fund III LP, with equity commitments of $518 million. With fund leverage, Freeport can invest about $960 million. The fund was seeking $500 million, according to a Securities and Exchange Commission filing. Arizona Public Safety Personnel Retirement System committed up to $100 million to the pool, according to a pension document. The vehicle will invest in senior-secured first-lien floating-rate loans to companies with annual revenue of $25 million to $100 million and earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization of $3 million to $25 million. The fund has invested about 35% of its capital. Freeport's previous fund collected $230 million in 2013, said a Moelis spokesman.

GSO Capital Partners, New York

GSO Capital Partners, the credit unit of Blackstone Group LP, gathered $6.5 billion, including leverage, for its third mezzanine fund, GSO Capital Opportunities Fund III LP. The firm has begun investing the fund, said a person familiar with the matter. The vehicle's final tally came in ahead of a $5 billion target indicated in due diligence notes from the New Mexico Educational Retirement Board, which approved a $125 million commitment to the fund this year. The vehicle also is larger than the $4 billion GSO collected for the fund's predecessor in 2012. Other investors that have disclosed commitments to the latest fund include the Texas Municipal Retirement System, Teachers Retirement System of Louisiana, San Francisco Employees' Retirement System and State of Michigan Retirement Systems. GSO plans to invest the fund across a range of sectors and geographies, with a particular focus on the U.S. and Europe. The firm typically focuses on companies with annual earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization of $75 million to $200 million, said a person familiar with the fund.

Neuberger Berman Group LLC, New York

Neuberger Berman Group LLC closed its second private-debt fund at $750 million, increasing the asset manager's private-credit business to $2.3 billion. NB Private Debt Fund II LP is larger than its predecessor fund, a $620 million vehicle that closed last year. The latest pool will invest in the primary issuances and secondary purchases of private equity-backed companies' junior debt, to aid private-equity firms in financing new buyouts and add-on acquisitions for portfolio companies as well as for refinancing needs. The fund, which is 28% invested in 15 companies, on average invests $50 million to $100 million. Susan Kasser, who co-manages the firm's private-credit business with David Lyon, said Neuberger Berman targets North American companies with $25 million to $250 million in earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization.

Oak Hill Advisors, New York

Credit specialist Oak Hill Advisors closed fundraising for OHA Strategic Credit Fund II LP at $2.7 billion, said a person familiar with the matter. The fund initially was seeking $2 billion, according to a May filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. Investors in the fund include Teachers' Retirement System of Louisiana and San Francisco Employees' Retirement System, according to pension documents. Like its predecessor, which closed with $1.13 billion in 2009, the new fund is expected to make both control and noncontrol investments mainly in corporate debt but will have the flexibility to invest in structured products as well as hard assets, another person familiar with the matter said. Oak Hill manages about $5 billion in its distressed strategies and roughly $30 billion overall following the fund's most recent close, the person said. The firm closed a $1.35 billion European distressed-debt fund in 2012.

Plexus Capital, Raleigh, N.C.

Debt investor Plexus Capital said it held a final closing for Plexus Fund IV with $400 million. The fund will invest in businesses with annual revenue of $10 million to $100 million. Its predecessor gathered $300 million in 2013. Plexus has raised more than $950 million across its four investment vehicles.

SECONDARY

HarbourVest Partners, Boston

HarbourVest Partners closed Dover Street IX LP, the investor's ninth secondary fund, with $4.77 billion, beating its $3.6 billion target. It originally had a $4.25 billion hard cap, Private Equity Analyst previously reported. Investors in the fund include the Ventura County Employees' Retirement Association, State of Michigan Retirement Systems, New Hampshire Retirement System, Nebraska Investment Council, Vermont Pension Investment Committee and Public School Teachers' Pension and Retirement Fund of Chicago. HarbourVest's Dover Street funds make large, complex secondary deals in less efficient parts of the market, in the U.S., Europe and Asia. The new vehicle is expected to invest in a range of private-equity stakes such as buyouts, growth equity and venture capital, and will make 25 to 40 deals of $75 million to $150 million each, according to a due diligence memo from consultant NEPC LLC for the Ventura County pension fund. The firm's eighth secondary vehicle closed at $3.6 billion in 2013.

VENTURE CAPITAL

Augment Ventures, Ann Arbor, Mich.

Augment Ventures has set out to raise $20 million for its second fund, Augment Ventures Fund II LP, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. Augment has invested in companies including UV-disinfection company RayVio Inc. and supply-chain software developer LLamasoft Inc. The firm, which launched in 2011, was seeking $20 million for its first fund, according to a separate SEC filing. It is unclear on what amount that fund closed.

Bowery Capital, New York

Bowery Capital, a firm formed by veterans of AOL Ventures, collected at least $58.7 million for its second fund, which has a $59.1 million offering amount, according to a regulatory filing. The firm closed its $33 million debut fund in 2013. Bowery makes early-stage investments in enterprise software startups. The firm's portfolio companies include data analytics companies mParticle and Premise Data Corp. and freight management company Transfix Inc.

Chicago Ventures, Chicago

Chicago Ventures closed its second seed-focused fund with $66 million. Chicago Ventures Fund II LP invested in 27 companies as of Oct. 31, almost half of them based in Chicago. The firm gathered $40 million for its first pool of capital in 2013.

Initialized Capital, San Francisco

Initialized Capital collected $102 million for its third fund, Initialized III LP, said Garry Tan, a managing partner at the firm. The firm focuses on preseed and seed funding deals with typical check sizes of $500,000 to $1 million in about 20 investments a year. Initialized is seeking $115 million for the fund, Mr. Tan said. It previously raised a first fund of $7 million and a $39 million second fund. Initialized can invest at the idea stage or as part of a seed round. So far, it has led about half of the seed rounds in which it has invested, Mr. Tan said.

Javelin Venture Partners, San Francisco

Javelin Venture Partners raised $125 million for its fourth fund, Javelin Venture Partners IV. The vehicle gathered the same amount it rounded up for its third pool of capital in 2013. The firm said that particular fund size is its "sweet spot," enabling it to invest in seed and Series A rounds as well as some Series B deals. Javelin writes initial checks of $250,000 to $6 million. GameCo Inc., a maker of video-game gambling machines, and LeadGenius, a provider of marketing software, are among its recent investments.

Linse Capital, Menlo Park, Calif.

Linse Capital, a late-stage investor in energy and transportation, has collected at least $22 million for its second fund, Linse Capital CP II LLC, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The firm collected at least $53.8 million for its first fund, which was seeking $75 million, according to an April SEC filing.

Massachusetts Institute of Technology, Cambridge, Mass.

Massachusetts Institute of Technology announced a startup accelerator that plans to raise a $150 million venture fund. The Engine will assist startups engaged in scientific and technological innovation with the potential to transform society. The program is aimed at highly technical projects in Greater Boston that might have languished in the lab because of lack of support and financial resources. It seeks to eventually support 60 startups at a time that will participate in its incubator for up to 12 months. MIT has committed $25 million to the accelerator's debut fund.

Maywic Select Investments, Cincinnati

Maywic Select Investments, which makes early- and growth-stage investments in consumer-product and retail companies that promote healthy lifestyles, is seeking $25 million for its second fund, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The firm didn't record any capital commitments for Maywic Select Investments II LP in the filing. Its predecessor vehicle was seeking $10 million, according to a 2015 SEC filing.

Moonrise Venture Partners, Greenwich, Conn.

Donald Pascal has attracted at least $90 million for a venture-capital fund with a $150 million offering amount, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The fund, Moonrise Venture Partners I LP, so far has two investors, according to the filing. Mr. Pascal previously was chief executive of Commonfund Capital.

Prairie Crest Capital, Des Moines, Iowa

Prairie Crest Capital, a new early-stage firm launched this year, aims to raise up to $100 million for its first fund, which will make agricultural technology investments, said principals Mark White and Barry Adams. Prairie Crest will seek investment opportunities emerging from the Midwest's universities and research institutions, but its focus will be national, its partners said. The new fund has an undisclosed family office as an anchor investor, and the firm expects to hold a first close in the first quarter of 2017, Messrs. White and Adams said. The vehicle has so far invested in one company: AgPixel LLC, which offers aerial imagery for farmers.

Precursor Ventures, San Francisco

Precursor Ventures, a preseed venture-capital firm, raised at least $15.2 million toward a fund with a $25 million offering amount, according to a regulatory filing. Precursor Ventures I LP, which focuses on investments in software companies, was originally set up by Charles Hudson to tap into funding through AngelList syndicates for follow-on investing in startups. Mr. Hudson also is a venture partner at SoftTech VC.

Quark Venture Inc., Vancouver, British Columbia

Quark Venture Inc. and investment bank GF Securities Co. said they are jointly establishing a $500 million global health-sciences venture fund. The vehicle will invest globally in a diversified portfolio of biotechnology and health-sciences companies. The fund has held a first closing on $100 million and is currently investing.

Questa Capital, San Francisco

Questa Capital is seeking $250 million for its debut fund, according to a filing with the Securities and Exchange Commission. The firm makes later-stage venture and growth-equity investments within the health-care services, health-care technology, digital-health, medical-technology and biopharmaceutical sectors. It didn't record any capital commitments for Questa Capital Partners I LP in the filing.

SJF Ventures, Durham, N.C.

SJF Ventures raised at least $74.4 million so far for a pair of funds with a combined offering amount of $125 million, according to filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission. SJF Ventures IV LP rounded up at least $68.2 million and companion fund SJF Ventures IVA LP closed on at least $6.2 million, according to the filings. The firm, which invests in technology, health care, clean energy, education, food and asset recovery, raised $90 million for its third fund in 2013. Recent investments include Portfolium Inc., a student talent marketplace; Ayla Networks Inc., a developer of technology to manage internet-of-things devices; and Solera Health Inc., which is building an online marketplace to combat diabetes.

Sofinnova Ventures, Menlo Park, Calif.

Biotechnology investor Sofinnova Ventures closed its 10th fund at its $650 million hard cap, exceeding the fund's initial $550 million target. Sofinnova Venture Partners X LP mainly will back mid- and later-stage drug developers. The fund's predecessor closed in 2014 with $500 million. Sofinnova expects to back 20 to 25 companies from the fund and to begin deploying the pool next year. General Partner Jim Healy said the new fund is bigger than its predecessor because the cost of drug development is increasing and because Sofinnova plans to invest in a slightly larger number of companies and to put a bit more money into them. The fund will invest $15 million to $35 million per company.

Third Rock Ventures, Boston

Third Rock Ventures raised $616 million for its largest fund aimed at launching and backing life-sciences startups. The firm began raising Third Rock Ventures IV LP over the summer and wrapped it up with one closing, partner Alexis Borisy said. Limited partners in the fund include undisclosed endowments, foundations, pensions, funds of funds and family offices, Mr. Borisy said. Third Rock expects to back 10 to 12 companies with the new pool. The fund's predecessor raised $516 million in 2013. It favors biotechnology companies with drug-development engines that can create multiple products and attract interest from pharmaceutical companies. In September, it launched Relay Therapeutics Inc. to develop treatments for cancer and other diseases based on a new understanding of the structural changes that proteins undergo.

Versant Ventures, San Francisco

Biotechnology investor Versant Ventures is seeking $350 million for Versant Venture Capital VI LP. Versant, a life sciences investor, makes bets on medical devices, drug discovery, pharmaceuticals and other biotechnology companies. Its last fund closed with $305 million in 2014. The firm was a top shareholder in Crispr Therapeutics at the time of the gene-editing specialist's public offering in October, holding 21% of the company's pre-IPO shares.

The firm will make additional hires to bolster the team.

The European Commission launched a venture-capital fund of funds with an anchor commitment of up to  ¬400 million ($441 million). The fund will invest in venture-capital funds across Europe and looks to draw at least  ¬1.2 billion in additional commitments from other sources. The European Union's investment will be capped at 25% of the vehicle's total investor commitments.

The European debt fund will invest its capital across a range of debt strategies, including high-yield bonds, leveraged loans and direct lending.

Scottish Equity Partners raised 260 million ($322 million) for its fifth fund to invest in technology companies, mainly in the U.K. and Ireland. SEP V closed above target, according to a statement from the firm. Investors in previous SEP funds accounted for almost 90% of commitments to the new vehicle. U.K. investors accounted for about 40% of commitments, with the remaining 60% contributed by investors based in Europe and the U.S. SEP V, which will follow a strategy similar to the firm's previous funds, will invest up to 20 million in growth-stage technology companies. Its previous fund reached a 200 million target in 2011.

Ysios said it now manages  ¬200 million across two funds. As with its predecessor, the fund will invest in biotechnology, medical-technology and diagnostics companies in Europe, with an emphasis on Spain. BUYOUTS
